<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1266661725">.mw-parser-output .portalbox{padding:0;margin:0.5em 0;display:table;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:175px;list-style:none}.mw-parser-output .portalborder{border:1px solid var(--border-color-base,#a2a9b1);padding:0.1em;background:var(--background-color-neutral-subtle,#f8f9fa)}.mw-parser-output .portalbox-entry{display:table-row;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;height:1.9em;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portalbox-image{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portalbox-link{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .portalleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portalright{clear:right;float:right;margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}}</style><ul role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portalbox portalborder portalright">
<li class="portalbox-entry"><span class="portalbox-image"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Socrates.png/20px-Socrates.png" decoding="async" width="18" height="28" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Socrates.png/40px-Socrates.png 1.5x" data-file-width="326" data-file-height="500" /></span></span></span><span class="portalbox-link"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Philosophy" title="Portal:Philosophy">Philosophy portal</a></span></li><li class="portalbox-entry"><span class="portalbox-image"><span class="skin-invert-image noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Psi2.svg/40px-Psi2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="28" height="28" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Psi2.svg/60px-Psi2.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="100" data-file-height="100" /></span></span></span><span class="portalbox-link"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Psychology" title="Portal:Psychology">Psychology portal</a></span></li></ul>
<p>The concept of metacognition has also been applied to collective teams and organizations in general, termed <a href="/wiki/Organizational_metacognition" title="Organizational metacognition">organizational metacognition</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metacognition&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Educational_psychology" title="Educational psychology">Educational psychology</a>&#160;– Branch of psychology concerned with the scientific study of human learning</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Educational_technology" title="Educational technology">Educational technology</a>&#160;– Use of technology in education to enhance learning and teaching</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Epistemology" title="Epistemology">Epistemology</a>&#160;– Philosophical study of knowledge</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goal_orientation" title="Goal orientation">Goal orientation</a>&#160;– Social-cognitive motivational disposition</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Introspection" title="Introspection">Introspection</a>&#160;– Examining one's own thoughts and feelings</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Learning_styles" title="Learning styles">Learning styles</a>&#160;– Largely debunked theories that aim to account for differences in individuals' learning</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Meta-emotion" title="Meta-emotion">Meta-emotion</a>&#160;– Emotions, and thoughts, about emotion</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Metaknowledge" title="Metaknowledge">Metaknowledge</a>&#160;– Knowledge about knowledge</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Metaphilosophy" title="Metaphilosophy">Metaphilosophy</a>&#160;– Investigation of the nature of philosophy</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchhausen_trilemma" title="Münchhausen trilemma">Münchhausen trilemma</a>&#160;– Thought experiment used to demonstrate the impossibility of proving any truth</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Metatheory" title="Metatheory">Metatheory</a>&#160;– Theory whose subject matter is itself a theory</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mentalization" title="Mentalization">Mentalization</a>&#160;– Ability to understand mental state that underlies behavior</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mindstream" title="Mindstream">Mindstream</a>&#160;– Buddhist concept of continuity of mind</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mirror_test" title="Mirror test">Mirror test</a>&#160;– Animal self-awareness test</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Phenomenology_(philosophy)" title="Phenomenology (philosophy)">Phenomenology (philosophy)</a>&#160;– Philosophical method and schools of philosophy</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Phenomenology_(psychology)" title="Phenomenology (psychology)">Phenomenology (psychology)</a>&#160;– Utilisation of analytic tools from phenomenology to study the human psyche</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Psychological_effects_of_Internet_use" title="Psychological effects of Internet use">Psychological effects of Internet use</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Second-order_cybernetics" title="Second-order cybernetics">Second-order cybernetics</a>&#160;– Application of cybernetics to itself</li></ul>
</div>

<li id="cite&#95;note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFColman2015" class="citation book cs1">Colman, Andrew M (2015). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.oxfordreference.com/view/10.1093/acref/9780199657681.001.0001/acref-9780199657681-e-5014">"metacognition"</a>. <i>A Dictionary of Psychology</i>. p.&#160;456. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1093%2Facref%2F9780199657681.001.0001">10.1093/acref/9780199657681.001.0001</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-965768-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-965768-1"><bdi>978-0-19-965768-1</bdi></a>. <q>Writings on metacognition can be traced back at least as far as <i>De Anima</i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Parva_Naturalia" title="Parva Naturalia">Parva Naturalia</a></i> of the Greek philosopher <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> (384-322 BC) [...].</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=metacognition&amp;rft.btitle=A+Dictionary+of+Psychology&amp;rft.pages=456&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft&#95;id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1093%2Facref%2F9780199657681.001.0001&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-965768-1&amp;rft.aulast=Colman&amp;rft.aufirst=Andrew+M&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.oxfordreference.com%2Fview%2F10.1093%2Facref%2F9780199657681.001.0001%2Facref-9780199657681-e-5014&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMetacognition" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
